<div id="analysis-of-activity-monitoring-data" class="section level1">
<h1>Analysis of Activity Monitoring Data</h1>
<div id="reproducible-research-peer-assignment-1" class="section level3">
<h3><strong>Reproducible Research : Peer Assignment 1</strong></h3>
<p><em>Kenneth Cheng</em></p>
<p><em>Jan 14 2015</em></p>
</div>
<div id="introduction" class="section level3">
<h3>Introduction</h3>
<p>This document presents an analysis of data collected at 5 minute intervals throughout a day from a personal activity monitoring device. The data is available in the coursera website for Reproducible Research Peer Assignment 1 <a href="https://d396qusza40orc.cloudfront.net/repdata%2Fdata%2Factivity.zip">Activity monitoring data</a>. The data consists of two months of data from an anonymous individual collected during the months of October and November 2012 and include the number of steps take in 5 minute intervals each day.</p>
<p>The report was produced using an R markdown document processed by knitr and then transformed into an HTML file.</p>
<p>The analysis of the imputed data, where missing values are replaced by the mean steps of the interval with missing values, show that median number of steps per interval increased a bit as compared to the non-imputed data. Moreover the number of steps over the weekend appears to have more occurences of above 100 steps per 5-minute intervals than on weekdays.</p>
</div>
<div id="data" class="section level3">
<h3>Data</h3>
<p>The data for this assignment was downloaded from the course website:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Dataset</strong>: <a href="https://d396qusza40orc.cloudfront.net/repdata%2Fdata%2Factivity.zip">Activity Monitoring data</a> [52K]</li>
</ul>
<p>The variables included in this dataset are:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><strong>steps</strong>: Number of steps taken in a 5-minute interval (missing values are coded as NA)</p></li>
<li><p><strong>date</strong>: The date on which the measurement was taken in YYYY-MM-DD format</p></li>
<li><p><strong>interval</strong>: Identifier for the 5-minute interval in which measurement was taken</p></li>
</ul>
<p>This dataset is stored in a comma-separated-value (CSV) file and there are a total of 17,568 observations in this dataset.</p>
</div>
<div id="loading-and-preprocessing-the-data" class="section level3">
<h3>Loading and preprocessing the data</h3>
<p>Load the data using read.csv()</p>
<pre class="r"><code>data &lt;- read.csv(&quot;activity.csv&quot;)</code></pre>
</div>
<div id="what-is-mean-total-number-of-steps-taken-per-day" class="section level3">
<h3>What is mean total number of steps taken per day?</h3>
<p>For this part of the assignment, you can ignore the missing values in the dataset.</p>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Make a histogram of the total number of steps taken each day</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>steps_per_day &lt;- aggregate(steps ~ date, data, sum)
hist(steps_per_day$steps, col=&quot;orange&quot;, main=&quot;Histogram of Total Steps Each Day&quot;, xlab=&quot;Number of Steps&quot;)</code></pre>

<ol start="2" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Calculate and report the mean and median total number of steps taken per day</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>rmean &lt;- mean(steps_per_day$steps)
rmedian &lt;- median(steps_per_day$steps)</code></pre>
<p>The mean number of steps taken per day is 1.076618910^{4} and median number of steps taken per day is 10765.</p>
</div>
<div id="what-is-the-average-daily-activity-pattern" class="section level3">
<h3>What is the average daily activity pattern?</h3>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Make a time series plot (i.e.type = l) of the 5-minute interval (x-axis) and the average number of steps taken, averaged across all days (y-axis)</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>steps_per_interval &lt;- aggregate(steps ~ interval, data, mean)
plot(steps_per_interval$interval, steps_per_interval$steps, type=&quot;l&quot;, xlab=&quot;Interval&quot;, ylab=&quot;Number of Steps&quot;, 
     main=&quot;Average Number of Steps per Day per 5-minute Interval&quot;)</code></pre>

title alt width="672" /></p>
<ol start="2" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Which 5-minute interval, on average across all the days in the dataset, contains the maximum number of steps?</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>max_interval &lt;- steps_per_interval[which.max(steps_per_interval$steps),1]
max_steps &lt;- round(max(steps_per_interval$steps))</code></pre>
<p>The 835th 5-minute interval contains the maximum number of 206 steps.</p>
</div>
<div id="inputing-missing-values" class="section level3">
<h3>Inputing missing values</h3>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Calculate and report the total number of missing values in the dataset(ie the total number of rows with NAs)</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>missing_vals &lt;- sum(is.na(data$steps))</code></pre>
<p>There are 2304 missing values in the dataset.</p>
<ol start="2" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Devise a strategy for filling in all of the missing values in the dataset. The strategy does not need to be sophisticated. For example, you could use the mean/median for that day, or the mean for that 5-minute interval, etc.</li>
</ol>
<p>Here we shall impute missing values by taking the average of the interval with missing values.</p>
<ol start="3" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Create a new dataset that is equal to the original dataset but with the missing data filled in.</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>data_i &lt;- merge(data, steps_per_interval, by = &quot;interval&quot;, suffixes = c(&quot;&quot;, &quot;.y&quot;))
nas &lt;- is.na(data_i$steps)
data_i$steps[nas] &lt;- data_i$steps.y[nas]
data_i &lt;- data_i[, c(1:3)]</code></pre>
<ol start="4" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Make a histogram of the total number of steps taken each day.</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>steps_per_day_i &lt;- aggregate(steps ~ date, data_i, sum)
hist(steps_per_day_i$steps, col=&quot;orange&quot;, main=&quot;Histogram of Total Steps Each Day for Imputed Data&quot;, xlab=&quot;Number of Steps&quot;)</code></pre>

title alt width="672" /></p>
<ol start="5" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Calculate and report the mean and median total number of steps taken per day.</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>mean_i &lt;- mean(steps_per_day_i$steps)
median_i &lt;- median(steps_per_day_i$steps)</code></pre>
<p>The mean is 1.076618910^{4} and median is 1.076618910^{4} for the total number of steps taken per day in the imputed data.</p>
<ol start="6" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Do these values differ from the estimates from the first part of the assignment?</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>mean_diff &lt;- mean_i - rmean
median_diff &lt;- median_i - rmedian</code></pre>
<p>The difference in the mean of imputed data from original data is 0. The difference in the median of imputed data from original data is 1.1886792.</p>
<ol start="7" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>What is the impact of imputing missing data on the estimates of the total daily number of steps?</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>total_diff &lt;- sum(steps_per_day_i$steps) - sum(steps_per_day$steps)</code></pre>
<p>The imputed data set resulted in 8.612950910^{4} more total daily number of steps.</p>
</div>
<div id="are-there-differences-in-activity-patterns-between-weekdays-and-weekends" class="section level3">
<h3>Are there differences in activity patterns between weekdays and weekends?</h3>
<ol style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Create a new factor variable in the dataset with two levels  weekday and weekend indicating whether a given date is a weekday or weekend day.</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>weekdays &lt;- c(&quot;Monday&quot;, &quot;Tuesday&quot;, &quot;Wednesday&quot;, &quot;Thursday&quot;, &quot;Friday&quot;)
data_i$dow = as.factor(ifelse(is.element(weekdays(as.Date(data_i$date)), weekdays), &quot;weekday&quot;, &quot;weekend&quot;))

steps_per_interval_i &lt;- aggregate(steps ~ interval + dow, data_i, mean)</code></pre>
<ol start="2" style="list-style-type: decimal">
<li>Make a panel plot containing a time series plot (i.e.type = l) of the 5-minute interval (x-axis) and the average number of steps taken, averaged across all weekday days or weekend days (y-axis). See the README file in the GitHub repository to see an example of what this plot should look like using simulated data.</li>
</ol>
<pre class="r"><code>library(lattice)
xyplot(steps_per_interval_i$steps ~ steps_per_interval_i$interval|steps_per_interval_i$dow, type=&quot;l&quot;, 
       main=&quot;Average Steps Per Day by Interval&quot;, xlab=&quot;Interval&quot;, ylab=&quot;Number of Steps&quot;, layout=c(1,2))</code></pre>
